(f)	No person shall allow or require a person in his employment under 18 years of age to dispense, serve, sell, or take orders for any alcoholic beverages. This subsection shall not prohibit persons under 18 years of age who are employed in supermarkets, convenience stores, breweries or drugstores from selling or handling alcoholic beverages which are sold for consumption off the premises. 
(g)	Testimony by any person under 21 years of age, when given in an administrative or judicial proceeding against another person for violation of any provision of this Code section, shall not be used in any administrative or judicial proceedings brought against such testifying person less than 21 years of age. 
(h)	In any case where a reasonable or prudent person could reasonably be in doubt as to whether or not the person to whom an alcoholic beverage is to be sold or otherwise furnished is actually 21 years of age or older, it shall be the duty of the person selling or otherwise furnishing, such alcoholic beverage to request to see and to be furnished with proper identification as provided for in subsection (d) of this section in order to verify the age of such person; and the failure to make such request and verification in any case where, the person to whom the alcoholic beverage is sold or otherwise furnished is less than 21 years of age may be considered by the trier of fact in determining whether the person selling or otherwise furnishing such alcoholic beverage did so knowingly. 
(i)	Any retailer or retail consumption dealer, or any person acting on behalf of such retailer or retail consumption dealer, who upon requesting proper identification from a person attempting to purchase alcoholic beverages from such retailer or retail consumption dealer pursuant to subsection (h) of this section is tendered a driver's license which indicates that such driver's license is falsified, is not the driver's license of the person presenting it, or that such person is under the age of 21 years, the person to whom said license is tendered shall be authorized to either write down the name, address, and license number or to seize and retain such driver's license and in either event shall immediately thereafter summon a law enforcement officer who shall be authorized to seize the license either at the scene or at such time as the license can be located. The procedures and rules connected with the retention of such license by the officer shall be the same as those provided for the acceptance of a driver's license as bail on arrest for traffic offenses pursuant to OCGA § 17-6-11. 
(j)	Violation of any provision of this section shall constitute an offense hereunder and shall be punishable in the municipal court; provided, violation of this section by a child shall be handled as provided by OCGA § 15-1-1 et seq. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-19. - Reserved. 
Sec. 3-20. - Duration and renewal of license. 
(a)	Generally. Except as otherwise provided, duration and renewal of licenses under this chapter shall be as for business licenses generally; and no licensee shall have any vested right to the renewal of any city license. No licenses under this chapter may be renewed if the licensee could be denied a new license under this chapter. In the case of the revocation or surrender of such license before the expiration of such license year, the holder thereof shall not be entitled to receive any refund whatsoever. 
(b)	All annual licenses renewal fees shall be paid on or before December 31 of each year or be charged a late penalty as set out hereafter. All fees will be accompanied by an application form as prescribed by the City Council of Lake Park which will be reviewed by the city clerk for any new (within the last year) infractions that would cast doubt as to whether the applicant should hold a license. Any licensee filing an application for renewal from January 1 until January 31 shall be charged a late penalty of 25 percent of the license fee to be paid in addition to the regular renewal fee. Any licensee filing an application for renewal from February 1 until February 28 shall be charged a late penalty of 50 percent of the license fee to be paid in addition to the regular renewal fee. An application for renewal filed after February 28 shall be treated as an original application must comply with all rules and regulation then in existence for new licenses. 
(c)	Expiration; renewal of distilled spirits licenses. Applicants in any given year for renewal of their licenses hereunder for the sale of distilled spirits for the next year shall file their application on or before the tenth day of December with the license inspector for the City of Lake Park. Upon payment of such fees and license taxes as are applicable on or before the 31st day of December, to the city, the license inspector shall issue the renewal license for the applicant. All licenses shall expire on the 31st day of December of the year for which they are issued, except when extended as provided in this chapter. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-21. - Distance and area requirements. 
(a)	No person shall be licensed by the city under this chapter for the retail sale of distilled spirits, malt beverages or wine where the parcel is located within 500 feet of any parcel upon which is located any of the following: 
(1)	Any public or private school;
(2)	Any public library;
(3)	Any church or similar place of worship;
(4)	Any child care or day care facility;
(5)	Any residence.
The distance will be measured as provided in section 3-1(5) of this chapter. 
(b)	No license shall be issued by the city under this chapter for consumption on the premises of distilled spirits, malt beverages, wine where the use of the property is a private club, as defined in section 3-101(5) or a supper club as defined in section 3-101(7) or a lounge as defined in section 3-101(3) and either use is located on a parcel within 300 feet of any parcel upon which is located any of the following: 
(1)	Any public or private school;
(2)	Any public library;
(3)	Any church or similar place of worship;
(4)	Any child care or day care facility;
(5)	Any residence.
The distance will be measured as provided in section 3-1(5) of this chapter. 
(c)	Except as is herein provided, no license shall be issued by the city under this chapter for consumption on the premises of distilled spirits, malt beverages or wine where the use of the property is a restaurant as a defined in section 3-101(6) or a hotel as defined in section 3-101(1) and either use is located on a parcel within 100 feet of a parcel upon which is located any of the following: 
(1)	Any public or private school;
(2)	Any public library;
(3)	Any child care or day care facility.
The distance will be measured as provided in section 3-1(5) of this Chapter. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-22. - Penalties; revocation of license. 
Any license under this chapter shall be subject to penalty and revocation for any conviction of the licensee or any agent, employee or officer thereof for violation of this chapter or any state law or regulation involving alcoholic beverages or sale of any illegal substance or article under the following procedure: 
(1)	Upon the conviction or entry of a plea of guilty or nolo contendere of a licensee or any agent, employee, or licensee thereof for a violation described in this section, the city clerk shall propose a penalty to be assessed against the licensee according to the following schedule: 
a.	For the first violation within the preceding 24 months, a fine of up to $5,000.00 and suspension of the license for up to seven days, or revocation. 
b.	For the second violation within the preceding 24 months, a fine of up to $10,000.00 and suspension of the license for up to 30 days, or revocation. 
c.	For the third violation within the preceding 24 months, a fine of up to $20,000.00 and/or revocation of the license. 
(2)	The city clerk shall cause to be served upon the licensee or any license agent thereof a written notice of the violation described in this section and the penalty proposed therefor. The licensee shall have five days from the date of service to request a hearing before the city council. Upon receipt of a request for a hearing, the city council shall provide by certified mail a notice to the licensee of the date, time and place of hearing, which date shall be not less than five days subsequent the date of such notice. At the hearing the licensee may present evidence and cross-examine opposing witnesses. 
(3)	Within five days after the hearing, or, if no hearing has been requested, after review of the proposed penalty, the city council shall issue a written decision either affirming, modifying or denying the proposed penalty. A copy of the written decision shall be provided to the licensee by certified mail and shall state the date and time of the next regular meeting of the city council at which the decision of the city council shall be presented for confirmation. 
(4)	The city council shall by resolution confirm, modify or deny the decision of the city clerk, or shall remand the action to the city clerk for further proceedings as may be directed. Following confirmation by the city council, the city clerk may cause the penalty to be imposed. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-23. - Employment of persons convicted of certain offenses; permits. 
(a)	It shall be unlawful for any licensee hereunder to employ in any premises used for the sale by the drink of alcoholic beverages, any person in any capacity whatsoever, including but not limited to performers, entertainers and musicians, who have been or has been, within three years prior to the date of such application for employment, convicted, served any sentence or other penalty or punishment, been on parole, or probation for a charge or violation of, soliciting for prostitution, pandering, letting premises for prostitution, keeping a disorderly place, illegally dealing in narcotics or other controlled substances, sex offenses, any crime involving moral turpitude or any felony. 
(b)	It shall be unlawful for any licensee hereunder to employ in any premises used for the sale of alcoholic beverages by the drink, any person in any capacity whatsoever, including but not limited to performers, entertainers and musicians, who have been or has been, within three years prior to the date of such application for employment, convicted on two or more occasions, or served any sentence or other penalty or punishment, been on parole or probation for a charge or violation relating to the manufacture or sale of alcoholic beverages of any type. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-24. - Outstanding licenses, compliance. 
(a)	So as to prevent an unconstitutional taking of property, all licensees for alcoholic beverages within the city in compliance with city ordinance requirements involving residency, distance, location, parking and type of building structure in effect at the time of first receiving the licenses and continuing to be in compliance therewith shall be exempt from the requirements of this chapter involving residency, distance, location, parking and type of building structure. 
(b)	Renewals and transfers of business ownership at the same location shall also be deemed in compliance hereunder to the extent provided in subsection (a) above. 
(c)	Business transfers to new locations and new licenses must comply with all requirements of this chapter. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-25. - Collection of taxes from distributors, wholesale dealers and manufacturers. 
At the time of delivery of any of such beverages as set out in this chapter such wholesale dealer, distributor or manufacturer shall collect from the retail dealer the taxes imposed by this chapter giving a correct and proper receipt therefor, and hold such taxes in trust for the city until the tax is remitted to the city as provided in this chapter. It shall be unlawful for any wholesaler, distributor, manufacturer or person to sell or deliver any such beverages as set out in this chapter to any retail dealer in the city, or for any such beverage to be transported into the city for resale by any means whatsoever, except to a licensed wholesale distributor, without collecting the taxes thereon as above set out at the time of sale or delivery. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-26. - Duties of retail dealers generally. 
All retail dealers in any of such beverages as set out in this chapter and all persons selling any of such beverages at retail within the city shall keep a correct record of all purchases and sales of each of such beverages, and shall demand of and require all persons from whom they purchase such beverages to furnish and deliver to them with such beverages, a correct invoice of each purchase, such invoice to be kept and preserved by such retailer at his place of business for a period of one year from the date of such purchase, and such invoices shall be open and subject to inspection by any authorized representative of the city at all reasonable times. Such retailer shall, on or before the close of business on the tenth business day of each month, make a report to the city clerk showing the number of containers of each and all such beverages purchased and/or sold during the previous month, and up to the close of business on the last business day of each month, showing the size and contents of each container, the name and address of all dealers and persons from whom purchases were made, the dates of delivery of same, and the amounts of total purchases such retailer has made from each wholesaler from whom such retailer has made purchases during the period covered by such statements. In addition, retailers licensed to sell alcoholic beverages by the drink for consumption on the premises shall make a report to the city clerk showing the total gross sales derived from the sale of distilled spirits by the drink. Gross sales shall include all credit card sales. The retailer shall accompany such reports with a remittance of all taxes due under this chapter for all purchases and sales made except those on which taxes have been paid to the manufacturer, distributor or wholesaler at the time of delivery as hereinbefore provided; and for all such taxes paid to such manufacturers, distributors or wholesalers such retailers shall furnish the city the proper original receipts showing the tax payment. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-27. - Refusal to make reports and remittances. 
If any wholesaler, distributor or retail dealer mentioned in this chapter fails or refuses to make the reports or remittances as provided herein and at the time specified, the license inspector shall notify such party in writing by mail, or otherwise, and if such reports are not made and the taxes paid within five days from the date of such notice, the license of the offending person shall stand revoked without further notice or cause, and the license inspector shall proceed to assess the amount of taxes due by such dealer from the best information available, plus ten percent thereof as a penalty, and cause an execution for the same to issue at once, and proceed to collect such taxes, penalty and cost as provided by ordinance for the collection of any other delinquent taxes, and in addition thereto make a case against such licensee in the municipal court for such offense. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-28. - Appeal hearing guidelines. 
Appeal hearing guidelines to read as follows: 
The city council is authorized to conduct an appeal hearing at the request of any applicant denied a license under this chapter or any licensee, license representative, employee or owner of a licensed establishment in the city whose license was suspended, probated, revoke or denied renewal. The licensee should be prepared to prove or show evidence of all business practices and procedures instituted to ensure compliance with this chapter and state law. The council inquiry may include, but is not limited to: 
(1)	Employment standards of the licensee;
(2)	Employee direction/supervision;
(3)	Sales procedures;
(4)	Training program (initial, recurrent, verification);
(5)	Enforcement check reports;
(6)	Previous violations;
(7)	Any other ordinance or law deemed relevant to the violation that is the subject matter of the hearing. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-29. - Procedure; right to counsel; cross examination of witnesses. 
(a)	Upon request for an appeal hearing to council, notice shall be sent to either the licensee or license representative personally or by certified mail at least 15 days, but no more than 45 days prior to the hearing date. Notice shall state the time, place and purpose of the hearing. 
(b)	The licensee shall be entitled to have counsel present at any hearing brought to inquire into suspension, revocation or probation of a license, and shall have the right to cross examine witnesses against him, and to produce evidence on his own behalf. 
(c)	Council will have present at said hearing any employee, agent or consultant that was involved in making the decision that is subject to the hearing. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Secs. 3-30—3-40. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - DISTILLED SPIRITS 

Secs. 3-41—3-60. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - RETAIL ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES 

Sec. 3-61. - Scope of article. 
In addition to the general business license requirements of this Code and article I of this chapter, the following sections shall apply to the licensing and operation of retail alcoholic establishments in the city; and should any section of this article conflict with other provisions in this chapter or the general business license requirements of this Code, then this article shall control. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-62. - Separation of alcoholic beverages for prohibition of sales during designated periods. 
All licensees hereunder shall provide a means of limiting access to alcoholic beverages, including malt beverages and/or wine, during times of prohibited sales, such as Sundays, or any other times of prohibited sales. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-63. - Employee regulations. 
An employee of a retail licensee shall meet the same character requirements as set forth in the general provisions of this chapter and pursuant to section 3-23 of this chapter. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-64. - Reserved. 
Sec. 3-65. - Excise tax on wholesale distributors of alcoholic beverages. 
(a)	The excise tax levied and imposed upon wholesalers for the selling of alcoholic beverages within the city, as contained further herein, shall be paid to the city as follows: 
(1)	Each wholesaler selling alcoholic beverages within the city shall file a report on the tenth day of each month showing for the preceding calendar month the exact quantities of alcoholic beverage, by size and type of container, constituting a beginning and ending period for the month, sold within the city, including an itemized report of purchases by each licensed establishment in the city. Each such wholesale dealer shall remit to the City of Lake Park, on the tenth day of the month next succeeding the calendar month in which such sales were made, the amount of excise tax due in accordance with this section. 
(2)	No decal, stamp or other identifying mark shall be required on malt beverages or wine sold within the city. 
(b)	The excise tax provided for hereinabove shall be in addition to any license fee, tax or charge which may now or in the future be imposed upon the business of selling malt beverages at retail or wholesale, within the corporate limits of the city. 
(c)	The failure to make a timely report and remittance shall render a wholesale dealer liable for a penalty equal to ten percent of the total amount due during the first 30-day period following the date such report and remittance were due and a further penalty of ten percent of the amount of such remittance for each successive 30-day period or any portion thereof, during which such report and remittance are not filed. The filing of a false or fraudulent report shall render the wholesale dealer making such report liable for a penalty equal to 50 percent of the amount of the remittance which would be required under an accurate and truthful statement or report and shall be grounds for revocation of the license of any dealer making such a report. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-66. - Reserved. 
Sec. 3-67. - License required for retail sale of alcoholic beverages; annual fee. 
It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation, club, society, association, or institution to have for sale at retail or to sell or offer for sale at retail, in the City of Lake Park, any alcoholic beverage without having first obtained a license to do so from the city. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-68. - Limitations on size and number of containers for retail sale. 
(a)	In retail establishments selling refrigerated (i.e. on ice or contained within an electric refrigeration system) alcoholic beverages and motor fuel: 
(1)	No refrigerated malt beverages may be sold in single containers equal to one quart or less except in packages of at least six such containers. 
(2)	No refrigerated wine may be sold in single containers of less than 750 ml.
(b)	The prohibitions of subsection (a) shall not apply to sales of such containers within a multiple package of identical containers prepared for retail sale by the brewer, distiller, distributor, or wholesaler and constituted of four or more units. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Secs. 3-69—3-80. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - CONSUMPTION ON THE PREMISES 

Secs. 3-81—3-91. - Reserved. 
Sec. 3-92. - Happy hour regulations. 
(a)	It is the intent and purpose of this section to prohibit activities typically associated with promotions referred to as "happy hour." 
(b)	No licensee or employee, or agent of a licensee, shall engage in any of the following practices in connection with the sale or distribution of alcoholic beverages for consumption on the premises: 
(1)	The giving away of any alcoholic beverage in conjunction with the sale of any other alcoholic beverage; 
(2)	The sale of two or more alcoholic beverages for a single price, including the sale of all such beverages a customer can or desires to drink at a single price; 
(3)	The sale or serving of two or more alcoholic beverages at substantially the same price customarily charged for one such alcoholic beverage; 
(4)	Requiring or allowing the purchase of a second or subsequent alcoholic beverage at the same time another alcoholic beverage is purchased or before the first such beverage has been consumed, by any one person. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-93. - Prohibited activities. 
No business under this article may promote, encourage or make available any activity that involves gambling. Gambling includes but is not limited to any activity where there is a chance for profit if a player is skillful or lucky; the act involves a payment of a price for a chance to win a prize or paying value against an uncertain event in hope of gaining something of value, typically in an amount beyond the amount originally paid. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-94. - Condition of premises. 
All licensed premises shall be kept clean and in proper sanitary condition, and in full compliance with the provisions and regulations governing the conditions of premises used for the storage and sale of food for human consumption. It shall be unlawful to permit any disturbance of the peace, or obscenity or any lewd, immoral or improper entertainment, conduct, or practices on such premises. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Secs. 3-95—3-100. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - LOUNGES, HOTELS AND RESTAURANTS 

Sec. 3-101. - Definitions. 
For the purposes of this article only the following terms shall have the meanings respectively ascribed to them, to wit: 
(1)	Hotel shall mean every building or other structure kept, used, maintained, advertised and held out to the public to be a place where food is actually served and consumed and sleeping accommodations are offered for adequate pay to travelers and guests, whether transient, permanent or residential, in which 50 or more rooms are used for the sleeping accommodations of such guests and having one or more public dining rooms, where meals are regularly served to such guests, such sleeping accommodations and dining rooms being conducted in the same building or in separate buildings or structures used in connection therewith that are on the same premises and are a part of the hotel operation. Motels meeting the qualifications set out herein for hotel shall be classified in the same category as hotels. Hotels shall have the privilege of granting franchises for the operation of a lounge, restaurant or supper club in their premises and the holder of such franchise shall be included in the definition of hotel hereunder. The public dining room connected herewith shall not be confused or defined with the definition of separate lounges, restaurants, private clubs or supper clubs as may be contained further herein, but in this instance, must be a dining room conducted in the same building or in separate buildings or structures used in connection therewith that are on the same premises and are a part of the hotel operation. The seating capacity for these hotel-connected facilities shall not be fixed as may be contained in further definitions herein. Further, the fee for the operation of any sale of alcoholic beverages shall be that fee as contained in section 3-146 of this chapter, and as relates to restaurants in connection with hotels, shall be determined by the seating capacity of 149 and below and 150 and above for the fee as designated in said section 3-146. 
(2)	Licensee shall mean a person, firm, corporation, association or establishment holding a license to engage in the retail sale of any and all alcoholic beverages by the drink for consumption on the licensed premises, and the annual license fees prescribed by this chapter includes any and all of such beverages sold by the drink by such licensee for consumption on the licensed premises. 
(3)	Lounge shall mean a separate room connected with, a part of, and adjacent to a restaurant or located in hotels or motels as defined herein, with all booths, stools and tables being open and unobstructed to the view of any other customers of, and in such lounge or the manager thereof. All lounges shall be air conditioned, and having a seating capacity of at least 50. A lounge, as defined herein, which is operated on a different floor in the premises, or in a separate building, or is not connected to or adjacent to a restaurant, shall be considered a separate establishment and shall pay an additional license fee therefor. 
(4)	Premises shall mean the lot and building thereon, closed or partitioned-in locality, whether room, shop or building wherein alcoholic beverages are sold by the drink, except in case of a hotel or motel premises. 
(5)	Private club shall be defined as contained in the definition under section 3-1, specifically subparagraph (10), as contained in this chapter. 
(6)	Restaurant shall mean any public place kept, used, maintained, advertised and held out to the public as a place where meals are served and where meals are actually and regularly served, without sleeping accommodations, such place being provided with adequate and sanitary kitchen and dining room equipment and seating capacity of at least 50 people, having employed therein a sufficient number and kind of employees to prepare, cook and serve suitable meals for consumption at tables in a dining room or dining rooms on the premises. Dining room(s) shall be staffed by a full service wait staff that will be responsible for the taking of the order at the table, delivering the order to the table, clearing the table and cashing out the bill. At least one meal per day shall be served at least six days a week, with the exception of holidays, vacations and periods of redecorating, and the serving of such meals shall be the principal business conducted, with the serving distilled spirits to be consumed on the premises as only incidental thereto. Said business must derive at least 50 percent of its total annual gross income from food and non-alcoholic beverage sales. 
(7)	Supper club shall mean those establishments having a seating capacity of at least 150 persons with all booths and tables being open to unobstructed view, and providing a band and/or other professional entertainment, a minimum of 20 days in each calendar month, each and every calendar month of a calendar year, with the exception of holidays, vacations and periods of redecorating. All such supper clubs shall be equipped with air conditioning, and shall maintain an adequate kitchen with a sufficient number of servants and employees for cooking, preparing, and serving food and meals for their patrons, and shall regularly serve at least one meal each day for six days each calendar week; provided, that supper clubs located in hotels or motels as defined herein having dining room and kitchen facilities may be relieved from maintaining a kitchen in connection with such supper club. The principal business of such supper clubs shall be entertainment, and any serving of alcoholic beverages shall be incidental thereto. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-102. - License constituted grant or privilege. 
Licenses hereunder shall be mere grants or privileges, and the City Council of Lake Park shall have the discretion to approve, or deny any application for a license to sell alcoholic beverages by the drink, or to revoke the same. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-103. - Sale without license. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to sell any alcoholic beverages for use or consumption on the premises without the license required herein. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-104. - Reserved. 
Sec. 3-105. - Residence requirements of applicants. 
Where the applicant for a license hereunder is a corporation, with an office and agent in this state, the license shall be issued to the corporation and its principal officer or agent residing in this state. For the purposes of this article, the agent may be the manager of the business at the applied for location. The agent for service may be different than the licensed agent at the licensed location. If the applicant is a partnership, the requirements of this section apply to all of the partners. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-106. - City official, spouse, children prohibited from holding license. 
It shall be unlawful for any elected or full or part time appointed employee or official of the state, county or city, or his or her spouse or minor child or children to hold any license hereunder. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-107. - Restrictions upon wholesalers of liquors. 
No person shall hold a license hereunder who also has any direct financial interest in any wholesale liquor business. No financial aid or assistance to any licensee hereunder from any wholesaler or manufacturer of intoxicating liquors shall be permitted. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-108. - Effect of prior conviction of crime upon applicant. 
No original license shall be issued to any person, partnership or corporation organized for pecuniary gain where any individual having an interest either as owner, partner or principal stockholder, directly or indirectly beneficial or absolute, or his spouse, shall have been convicted, or shall have entered a plea of nolo contendere within ten years immediately prior to the filing of said application, for any felony or misdemeanor of any state or of the United States or any municipal ordinance except traffic violations; the term "conviction" shall include an adjudication of guilty or a plea of guilty or nolo contendere or the forfeiture of a bond when charged with such a crime or violation. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-109. - Surveyor's drawing to accompany application for license. 
All applications for an original or new license shall include a certificate from a registered surveyor showing a scaled drawing of the location of the proposed premises, and the distance as measured in section 1-1(5) from the proposed licensee's location to the nearest church building, school building, residence or public library; provided this section shall not apply to a hotel or motel as a licensee hereunder if all alcoholic sales and consumption are on or above a second story level from the adjacent street level. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-110. - Forms, data, information, records for license application. 
The City Council of Lake Park shall prescribe forms for new or renewal applications hereunder. All applicants shall furnish all data, information and records requested of them by the police committee or the police department, and failure to furnish such data, information, and records within 30 days from the date of such request shall automatically be cause to dismiss, with prejudice, such applications. Applicants, by filing an application, agree to produce for oral interrogation any person or persons requested by the police committee or police department and considered by such committee or department as being important in the ascertainment of the facts relative to the grant of such license. The failure to produce such person or persons within 30 days after being requested to do so shall result in the automatic rejection of such application. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-111. - Untrue, misleading information in license application. 
Any material untrue or misleading information contained in, or material omission left out of an original, renewal, or transfer application for a license hereunder shall be cause for the denial thereof, and, if any license has been granted under such circumstances, shall be cause for the revocation of the same. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Secs. 3-112, 3-113. - Reserved. 
Sec. 3-114. - Registration of new applications for licenses. 
New or original applications hereunder shall be dated with the time of filing with the city clerk, and shall be designated by an "S" for supper clubs, "R" for restaurants, "H" for hotels and motels and "O" for others, followed by a number to designate the order of filing, the numbers to begin anew with each calendar year; preference shall be given, in each category, whenever feasible, to the order in which the applications are filed. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-115. - License not to issue to applicant not meeting requirements herein. 
No license shall issue to any applicant who does not meet the requirements of a restaurant, hotel, motel, private club, lounge or supper club as defined herein. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-116. - Reserved. 
Sec. 3-117. - Due date for license fees; prorating license fees. 
All annual license renewal fees hereunder shall be paid on or before December 31 of each year or be charged a late penalty as provided in section 3-120. Any new license granted hereunder shall pay the full license fee without proration, except that the fee for a new license granted after June 30 in any calendar year shall be 50 percent of the above-stated annual license fees for the remainder of that calendar year. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-118. - Time limit for obtaining license, paying fee. 
All licenses must be obtained and fees therefor paid not later than two weeks from the date of the approval of the application by the City of Lake Park, and if not so obtained, the existing permit shall be void. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-119. - Duration of license; refunds. 
No license shall issue for less than a calendar year period, or the remainder thereof, except as otherwise provided in this article. In the case of the revocation or surrender of such license before the expiration of such calendar year period, the holder thereof shall not be entitled to receive any refund whatsoever. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-120. - Renewal of licenses. 
All licensees hereunder shall be required to apply for and renew their licenses annually on forms prescribed by the City Council of Lake Park. Any licensee filing an application for renewal from January 1 until January 31 shall be charged a late penalty of 25 percent of the license fee to be paid in addition to the regular renewal fee. Any licensee filing an application for renewal from February 1 until February 28 shall be charged a late penalty of 50 percent of the license fee to be paid in addition to the regular renewal fee. When any such licensee fails to file his application on or before the 28th day of February, any application thereafter shall be treated as an original application for a new license and not for a renewal. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-121. - Forfeiture of license for nonuse. 
(a)	Failure to open for business. All holders of licenses hereunder must within nine months after the issuance of the license open for business the establishment referred to in the license, and begin the sale of the product or products authorized by the license. Failure to open the proposed establishment, and begin the sale referred to above within the nine-month period shall serve as automatic forfeiture and cancellation of the unused license, and no refund of license fees shall be made to the license holder. 
(b)	Cessation of business. Any license issued under this chapter shall automatically be null and void where the licensed business has not operated or been open to the public for six consecutive months. Said license shall automatically become null and void and be of no further force or effect without the necessity of any action of the clerk, city manager or city council. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-122. - Suspension, revocation of license. 
(a)	Grounds, hearing required. No license which has been issued or which may hereafter be issued by the city hereunder, which has not expired under provisions of this article, shall be suspended or revoked, except for due cause, as herein defined, after a hearing upon five days prior written notice to the holder of such license of the time, place and purpose of such hearing, and a statement of the reasons for such hearing. 
(b)	Due cause defined. "Due cause" for the suspension or revocation of such license shall consist of conviction in a court of competent jurisdiction of fraud in obtaining it, the violation of any laws or ordinances regulating such businesses, or violation of regulations made pursuant to authority granted for the purpose of regulating such businesses, or conviction of a felony under any state or federal law. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-123. - Violation of article constitutes grounds for revocation of license. 
Any violation of any provision of this article by the holder of a license hereunder or designee shall be subject to any penalties or sanction set forth in section 3-22. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-124. - Reserved. 
Sec. 3-125. - Distance requirements from church, school, residence. 
The distance requirements as contained in section 3-21 shall apply to licensees hereunder; provided that after careful consideration of the proposed location, the city council may waive the distance requirements herein for hotels and motels as defined herein. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-126. - Prohibited activities. 
No business under this article may promote, encourage or make available any activity that involves gambling. Gambling includes but is not limited to any activity where there is a chance for profit if a player is skillful or lucky; the act involves a payment of a price for a chance to win a prize or paying value against an uncertain event in hope of gaining something of value, typically in an amount beyond the amount originally paid. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-127. - Condition of premises. 
All licensed premises shall be kept clean and in proper sanitary condition, and in full compliance with the provisions and regulations governing the conditions of premises used for the storage and sale of food for human consumption. It shall be unlawful to permit any disturbance of the peace, or obscenity or any lewd, immoral or improper entertainment, conduct, or practices on such premises. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-128. - Standards for prescribed sleeping or seating capacity; applicability of fire regulations. 
Where a minimum sleeping or seating capacity is prescribed herein, the same shall be judged by existing ordinances, or by reasonable standards. The fire department shall, upon request of the police committee, inspect such premises and report their findings to the committee. All premises licensed hereunder shall conform at all times to all fire regulations of the city. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-129. - Reserved. 
Sec. 3-130. - Service of drinks to be by employees only. 
Drinks sold hereunder shall be served only by employees of the licensee hereunder. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-131. - Regulations to be posted, employees to be instructed as to contents thereof. 
It shall be the duty of the licensee hereunder to maintain a copy of this article on such premises, and to instruct each and every employee of the terms hereof. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-132. - Prohibited activities by employees. 
It shall be unlawful for an employee of a supper club or lounge to dance or sit with customers in the premises, or for any customer to be permitted to purchase food or drink for such employees in such premises. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-133. - Employment of minors. 
No licensee hereunder shall employ a minor in his establishment except under the conditions as provided in section 3-18 of this chapter; provided that musicians and other entertainers 18 years of age may provide professional entertainment upon the premises of the licensee. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-134. - Reserved. 
Sec. 3-135. - Serving drinks on trains, airplanes. 
Nothing herein shall prohibit the serving of distilled spirits by the drink on dining or club cars of trains or on airplanes in transit on regular schedules. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-136. - Reserved. 
Sec. 3-137. - Sale to minors or incapacitated persons; loitering about premises. 
No licensee hereunder shall sell alcoholic beverages to or allow any persons under 21 years of age or incapacitated persons to be in, frequent or loiter about the licensed premises of a supper club or lounge; provided, however, persons under 21 years of age may frequent or be in such supper clubs or lounges if they are accompanied by a parent or legal guardian. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-138. - Misrepresentation of age, possession, consumption by minors. 
(a)	It shall be unlawful for any person under 21 years of age to misrepresent his age in any manner whatsoever to a licensee hereunder. 
(b)	It shall be unlawful for any person under 21 years of age to drink or possess any alcoholic beverage as defined herein on any licensed premises. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-139. - Package sales by licensees. 
Licenses hereunder shall not permit the sale of distilled spirits by the bottle or package. Such persons holding such licenses shall have the right to sell wines, champagnes or malt beverages to the public by the bottle or package for consumption on the premises without the issuance of a separate retail license therefor. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-140. - Opened original packages on licensed premises prohibited. 
It shall be unlawful for any person except a licensee, his manager or agent in charge of any licensed premises hereunder to carry into or have in his possession on any licensed premises, any alcoholic beverage in the original package the seal of which has been broken or the original package opened. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-141. - Misrepresenting quantity, quality of bottle. 
It shall be illegal for licensees hereunder to add to the contents of a bottle, or to refill empty bottles, or in any other manner to misrepresent the quantity, quality or brand name of any alcoholic beverages. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-142. - Service in back rooms prohibited. 
The sale of alcoholic beverages for consumption by persons in any back room or side room which is not open to general public use is prohibited, except that private parties or conventions, which have been scheduled in advance, may be served in public or private dining rooms or meeting rooms; and provided further, that this prohibition shall not apply to private clubs hereunder, nor to the sale of alcoholic beverages for consumption hereunder to the registered guest of any hotel or motel in their designated and private rooms. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-143. - Sales outside premises. 
It shall be unlawful for any sales to be made outside of the premises on the lot on which such business is licensed for such sale, except as permitted herein. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-144. - Acts prohibited unless licensed. 
It shall be illegal and an offense against the ordinances of the city for any person, firm, corporation, association, society, union, institution, private club, or other form of organization, or any combination thereof, without having applied for, and obtained a annual license to sell at retail alcoholic beverages by the drink for consumption on the premises where such sale occurs, to engage or continue in any of the following activities or conduct: 
(1)	Selling alcoholic beverages at retail by the drink for consumption on the premises where sold for such consumption; 
(2)	Selling at retail alcoholic beverages for consumption by the drink on the premises where such retail sale occurs; 
(3)	Controlling or possessing alcoholic beverages for retail sale by the drink for consumption on the premises where controlled or possessed for such retail sale; 
(4)	Offering alcoholic beverages for sale at retail by the drink for consumption on the premises where offered; 
(5)	Furnishing alcoholic beverages, to be served by the drink, at retail for consumption on the premises where so furnished; 
(6)	Storing or keeping, or permitting the storage or keeping of broken or unsealed packages of alcoholic beverages of members for consumption thereof by the owners of such liquors on the premises where so stored or kept; 
(7)	Acquiring, delivering, receiving or accepting alcoholic beverages by any one at or on any premises other than his or her bona fide home for consumption thereat or therein, if no city license for the retail sale of such beverage at such place by the drink is in effect; 
(8)	Providing a room, place, or premises for keeping or storage, of sealed and unopened, or opened or unsealed containers or bottles of alcoholic beverages for sale at retail, or for consumption thereof on such premises when no valid city license to retail alcoholic beverages by the drink for consumption on such premises shall be in force; 
(9)	Evading any provision of this or any other valid ordinance of this city relating to the retail sale of alcoholic beverages by the drink for consumption on the premises where sold, served, or furnished for consumption on such premises, by whatever false scheme, trick or device may be employed; 
(10)	Making gratuitous gifts or donations of spurious memberships in an alleged private, regular, dues-paying members club, or including enough not specified in the price charged for purchases of merchandise or privileges, other than distilled spirits, to cover membership dues, shall be held an evasion, and shall not be treated as a bona fide donation or gift; 
(11)	Aiding, abetting, counseling, advising, or assisting in the violation of this or any other applicable valid city ordinance relating to the sale at retail of any alcoholic beverage by the drink for consumption on the premises where sold. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
Sec. 3-145. - Private clubs defined. 
(a)	In addition to the definition as provided in section 3-1(10) of this chapter, a private membership club, within the meaning of this section, shall be and is hereby defined as only such organizations as: 
(1)	Cannot limit or restrict the authority, control, or power of one of its members within three months from the date he becomes such member; or 
(2)	Shall make and keep a correct and true printed or typewritten list of all of its members open to inspection of the city license inspector, mayor, all members of the city council, the city manager, and any member of the police department of the city, at all times of day and night when the club is open to its members; and 
(3)	Confine its membership to persons over 21 years of age; and
(4)	Restricts their patronage to their bona fide regular dues-paying members; and
(5)	Derive the most of their income from their bona fide regular membership dues, sales and service of meals, and private dances by such members and their immediate families, or other lawful activities not related to or involving the sale or use of distilled spirits; and 
(6)	Do not derive their chief income from the sale of alcoholic beverages.
(b)	The prohibitions contained in section 3-144 shall specifically apply herein. 
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011)
ARTICLE VI. - LICENSE FEES AND EXCISE TAXES 

Sec. 3-146. - Schedule of license fees and excise taxes. 
There shall be an application fee of $100.00 for all applications for a new alcoholic beverage license. Applicants applying for more than one type of license at the same time shall only be required to pay one application fee. The application fee shall not apply to applications to renew existing licenses. In addition to any other business license fees that may be applicable under this Code, the following annual license taxes shall be paid for the type of license being acquired as follows: 
(1)	License fee for on-premises consumption of:
a.	Malt beverages: .....$165.00 
b.	Wine: .....$165.00 
c.	Distilled spirits: .....$2,920.00 
d.	Sunday sales of alcoholic beverages by the drink for consumption on the premises (in addition to all licenses to sell alcoholic beverages by the drink): .....$500.00 
(2)	License fee for package sale (no on-premises consumption) of malt beverages: .....$165.00 
(3)	License fee for package sale (no on-premises consumption) of wine: .....$165.00 
(4)	License fee for package sale (no on premises consumption) of distilled spirits: .....$2,920.00 
(4.1)	License fee for Sunday package sales of beer, wine and/or distilled spirits (no on premises consumption, in addition to all regular licenses for package sales): .....$500.00 
(5)	License fee for on-premises consumption of malt beverages and wine at private membership club: .....$400.00 
a.	Sunday sales of alcoholic beverages by the drink for consumption on the premises at private membership club (in addition to all licenses to sell alcoholic beverages by the drink): .....$500.00 
(6)	Excise tax upon wholesalers selling malt beverages within the city per 12-ounce container or fraction thereof: .....0.05 
Or, per ounce of malt beverage sold by each wholesale dealer within the corporate limits of the city: .....0.0041 
(7)	Excise tax upon distilled spirits wholesalers: $0.22/liter, excluding fortified wines, and a proportionate tax at the same rate for all fractional parts of a liter. 
(8)	Excise tax upon retail sales of distilled spirits by the drink: Three percent of the charge to the public for the beverages. 
(9)	Excise tax upon all retail dealers of wine in the amount of: $0.22/liter and a proportionate tax at the same rate for all fractional parts of a liter, except that the following shall be exempt from tax: 
a.	Wine sold to and used by established and recognized churches and synagogues for use in sacramental services only; 
b.	Any wine exempt from taxation by the state under the United States Constitution;
c.	Wine sold to persons outside this state for resale or consumption outside this state; and 
d.	Wine containing less than one-half of one percent alcohol by volume.
(Ord. No. 104, 1-4-2011; Ord. No. 104 Amd 1, § II, 5-5-2015)
Chapter 4 - ANIMALS AND FOWL[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Creation of noise by animals, § 7-3(7).
State Law reference— Livestock running at large or straying, OCGA § 4-3-1 et seq.; abandonment of dogs, OCGA § 4-8-3; liability of owner, etc., for damages done to livestock or poultry by dog, OCGA § 4-8-4; control of rabies, OCGA § 3-19-1 et seq.; licensing and regulations of animals of local authorities, OCGA § 31-19-3; notice when person bitten by animal suspected of being rabid, OCGA § 31-19-4.

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 4-1. - Livestock or poultry at large prohibited. 
It shall be unlawful for the owner, or any other person having possession of any cow, horse, mule, hog, sheep or goat, or any poultry, to allow such animal or poultry to run at large in any street or public place within the city. 
Sec. 4-2. - Proximity of livestock to residence—Minimum distance of keeping; declaration of nuisance. 
It shall be unlawful for any owner, or any other person having possession of any cow, horse, mule, sheep or goat, to stable or otherwise confine any such animal in the city within 100 yards of any dwelling wherein a person resides; the violation of which is declared to be a nuisance likely to endanger the public health. 
Sec. 4-3. - Same—Minimum distance of pens or enclosures. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to maintain a stable, pen, or other place of confinement for the keeping of cows, horses, mules, sheep or goats within 100 yards of any dwelling wherein a person resides; the violation of which is hereby declared to be a nuisance likely to endanger the public health. 
Sec. 4-4. - Minimum area per three head of livestock. 
It shall be unlawful for any owner, or other person having possession of, any cows, horses, mules, sheep or goats, to stable or confine more than three of such animals together within an enclosure containing less than 500 square yards; the violation of which is declared to be a nuisance likely to endanger the public health. 
Sec. 4-5. - Swine prohibited. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to keep swine in the city; the violation of which is declared to be a nuisance likely to endanger the public health. 
Sec. 4-6. - Nuisance control. 
Without regard to other provisions of this chapter or other sections of the Lake Park Code, it shall be unlawful for owners of dogs, cats or other animals to allow, permit or by negligence fail to prevent such animals from acting or performing in such a manner as to cause damage or insanitary conditions to the property of another or otherwise to cause a nuisance in Lake Park. Acts deemed to be nuisances shall include but are not limited to the following: 
(1)	Dogs or cats entering any place where a food is stored, prepared, served or sold to the public except "Seeing Eye" dogs while in the company of a blind person. 
(2)	Any dog chasing, running after or jumping at vehicles moving on public streets and alleys. 
(3)	Any dog habitually snapping, growling, snarling, jumping upon or otherwise threatening persons lawfully using the public sidewalks, streets, alleys or other public ways or habitually attacking other animals. 
(4)	Any animal howling, yelping, whining or barking in such manner as to reasonably disturb any person or neighborhood. 
(5)	Any dog feeding from, turning over or otherwise disturbing garbage containers.
(6)	Any animal scratching or digging in flower beds or soiling or damaging the property of anyone other than the owner. 
(7)	Male animals having access to female animals or vice versa during a breeding season except within enclosures so arranged as to obstruct such animals entirely from the view of persons outside such enclosures. 
(8)	Dogs running at large not on a leash or in voice control of a person and having access to yards or property of persons other than that of the owner of such dog. 
(Ord. No. 3 Amd. 1, 10-6-87)
Sec. 4-7. - Violations and penalties for sections 4-6, 4-25 and 4-29. 
Any person violating the provisions of sections 4-6, 4-25, or 4-29 and convicted in municipal court shall receive a $150.00 fine and/or 30 days' confinement in the county jail and contempt of court. Also, should the provisions of section 4-29 be violated, identified vicious dogs will be confined at the county pound at the owner's expense as directed by the municipal court. 
(Ord. No. 3 Amd. 1, 10-6-87)
Secs. 4-8—4-19. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - DOGS; RABIES CONTROL 

Sec. 4-20. - Definitions. 
As used in this article, the following terms shall have the respective meanings ascribed to them: 
Dog means a canine animal of either sex. 
Dog under control means a dog is under control if he is controlled by a leash, is at heel, or is beside a competent person and obedient to that person's commands, or is within a vehicle being driven or parked on the streets, or is within the property limits of his owner or custodian. 
Sec. 4-21. - Enforcement of article. 
The governing body may enforce this article, or may negotiate with and contract with the county for the purpose of cooperating with the county in the enforcement of this article; and may enter into contracts with the county to provide for a dog catcher and dog pound facilities all in furtherance of the enforcement of this article. 
Sec. 4-22. - Identification and vaccination—Required. 
It shall be unlawful for any owner or custodian of a dog to keep such dog without a collar which shall have attached a valid vaccination tag as required by the law of the state, and identification tag showing the name and address of the owner or custodian of said dog. 
Sec. 4-23. - Same—Illegal attachment or removal of tag. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to attach a vaccination or identification tag to any dog for which it was not intended, or to remove a vaccination or identification tag or collar from any dog without the consent of its owner or custodian. 
Sec. 4-24. - Same—Qualifications to vaccinate. 
No person shall vaccinate dogs against rabies who is not licensed to practice veterinary medicine in the state. 
Sec. 4-25. - Dogs at large prohibited. 
Irrespective of and/or in addition to impoundment provisions, including assessment of penalty fees relating to impoundment of animals as prescribed in other sections of this chapter, it shall be unlawful for owners of dogs to allow, permit, or by negligence fail to prevent their dogs from running at large not on a leash or in voice control of a responsible person. Any dog on the owner's property and not confined thereto by fence, chain, or other suitable and effective means, and when no responsible person is present to control such dog, shall be considered running at large and in violation of this chapter. 
(Ord. No. 3, § 1, 8-7-73; Ord. No. 3 Amd. 1, 10-6-87)
Sec. 4-26. - Impounding—Required as to dogs in violation. 
Any dog found running at large in violation of this article shall be immediately impounded by the duly authorized officers and agents of the city. 
Sec. 4-27. - Same—Impounding; costs; redemption. 
(a)	The chief of police shall have the authority to impound any dogs found at large on the streets. Such officer shall charge the owner for the actual cost to the city of impounding and upkeep of the dog. 
(b)	If the owner of the dog does not reclaim the impounded dog within ten days the chief of police may dispose of the same. 
(Ord. No. 3, §§ 2, 3, 8-7-73)
Sec. 4-28. - Same—Authority when owner unknown. 
In the event that the owner or custodian of a dog is not known, and such dog is upon the streets, alleys, sidewalks, school grounds, public places, and premises of another, any law enforcement officer or agent or employee duly authorized by the city shall be authorized to take possession of such dog and impound it in accordance with the rules and regulations now or hereinafter provided by law or by ordinance of the city for the detention, control and disposition of dogs impounded pursuant to applicable law or ordinance. 
Sec. 4-29. - Vicious dogs. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to cause, permit, accompany or be responsible for the presence of any vicious dog on the streets of the city or in any other public place therein, at any time, unless and in addition to the other requirements of this article, such dog shall be securely muzzled or confined to effectively prevent it from biting any person or other animal. Biting is defined as breaking of the skin of a person or animal by the teeth of the dog. In addition, any vicious dog which attacks a human being or another domestic animal may be ordered destroyed when, in the court's judgment, such vicious dog represents a continuing threat of serious harm to human beings or domestic animals. 
(Ord. No. 3 Amd. 1, 10-6-87)
Chapter 5 - BUILDINGS AND CONSTRUCTION[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Charter reference— Authority to enact rules and regulations, and to adopt codes, § 7.22.
Cross reference— Fire prevention, Ch. 6.5; cleanliness of premises, § 7-20 et seq.; utilities and services, Ch. 14.
State Law reference— State building, plumbing, electrical, etc., codes, OCGA § 8-2-20 et seq.; application of building and fire related codes to existing buildings, OCGA § 8-2-200 et seq.; adoption of ordinances relating to land-disturbing activities, OCGA § 12-7-4; building permits and certificates of occupancy for buildings presenting special hazards to persons or property, OCGA § 25-2-14; electrical contractors, plumbers and conditioned air contractors, OCGA § 43-14-1 et seq.

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 5-1. - Building inspector—Office created; appointment, acting official. 
(a)	The office of building inspector is hereby created.
(b)	The building inspector shall be appointed by the mayor, with the consent of the council. His appointment shall be for one year, unless sooner removed. 
(c)	During temporary absence or disability of the building inspector the appointing authority shall designate an acting building inspector, and shall include his duly authorized assistants. 
Sec. 5-2. - Same—Duties. 
It shall be the duty of the building inspector to enforce all laws relating to the construction, alteration, removal, and demolition of buildings and structures. 
Sec. 5-3. - Same—Right of entry. 
The building inspector, in the discharge of his official duties and upon proper identification, shall have authority to enter any building, structure or premises at any reasonable hour. 
Sec. 5-4. - Appeals. 
From a denial of a building permit or other adverse decision by the building inspector, any party may appeal to the governing body. 
Sec. 5-5. - Duties of property owner. 
It is the duty of the owner of every dwelling, building, structure, or property within the city to construct and maintain such dwelling, building, structure, or property in conformance with applicable codes in force within the city, or such ordinances which regulate and prohibit activities on property and which declare it to be a public nuisance to construct or maintain any dwelling, building, structure, or property in violation of such codes or ordinances. 
State Law reference— O.C.G.A. § 41-2-9(a)(1). 
Secs. 5-6—5-19. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - HOUSING CODE 

Sec. 5-20. - Adoption; penalty. 
For the purpose of maintaining the health and cleanliness of the city by establishing minimum housing standards and providing for abatement of nuisances within the city, there is hereby adopted as the housing code of the city that certain housing code promulgated by the Southern Building Code Congress International, Inc., Birmingham, Alabama, being particularly the Standard Housing Code, 1985 edition, save and except such portions as are hereinafter stricken or modified, or are in conflict with this Code of Ordinances, and from the date on which this section shall take effect the same shall be controlling within the jurisdiction of the city. At least one copy thereof is on file in the office of the city clerk. 
Any person violating said code shall be subject to punishment as provided in section 1-8. 
(Ord. of 1-6-76)
State Law reference— Adoption and continuation of state minimum standard codes, OCGA § 8-2-21. 
Secs. 5-21—5-29. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - DANGEROUS STRUCTURES[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference— Abating nuisance structures, OCGA § 41-2-7 et seq.

Sec. 5-30. - Definitions. 
As used in this article: 
Closing means securing and causing a dwelling, building, or structure to be vacated. 
Dwellings, buildings, or structures means any building or structure or part thereof used and occupied for human habitation, commercial, industrial, or business uses, or intended to be so used, and includes any outhouses and appurtenances belonging thereto or usually enjoyed therewith and also includes any building or structure of any design. 
Owner means the holder of the title in fee simple and every mortgagee of record. 
Municipal court means the Municipal Court for the City of Lake Park, Georgia. 
Parties in interest means persons in possession of the property and all individuals, associations, and corporations who have interest of record in the county where the property is located in a dwelling, building, or structure, including executors, administrators, guardians, and trustees. 
Public authority means any housing authority or any officer who is in charge of any department or branch of the government of the municipality, county, or state relating to health, fire, or building regulations or to other activities concerning dwellings, buildings, or structures in the municipality. 
Public officer means the city marshal, the city building inspector and such officer or officers who are authorized by this article to exercise the powers prescribed herein, or any agent of such officer of officers. 
Repair means closing a dwelling, building, or structure or the cleaning or removal of debris, trash, and other materials present and accumulated which create a health or safety hazard in or about any dwelling, building, or structure. 
(Ord. No. 84, § I, 11-2-04)
Sec. 5-31. - Powers of city officer in regard to unfit buildings or structures. 
An officer properly authorized by the city may exercise the powers necessary or convenient to carry out and effectuate the purpose and provisions of this article, including the following powers in addition to others herein granted: 
(1)	To investigate the dwelling conditions in the city in order to determine which dwellings, buildings, or structures therein are unfit for human habitation or are unfit for current commercial, industrial, or business use; 
(2)	To administer oaths and affirmations, to examine witnesses, and to receive evidence;
(3)	To enter upon premises for the purpose of making examinations; provided, however, that such entries shall be made in such manner as to cause the least possible inconvenience to the persons in possession; 
(4)	To appoint and fix the duties of such officers, agents, and employees as he deems necessary to carry out the purposes of this article; and 
(5)	To delegate any of his functions and powers under this article to such officers and agents as he may designate. 
Sec. 5-32. - Determination by public officer that dwelling, building, or structure is unfit. 
A public officer may determine that a dwelling, building, or structure is unfit for human habitation or is unfit for its current commercial, industrial, or business use if he finds that conditions exist in such building, dwelling, or structure which are dangerous or injurious to the health, safety, or morals of the occupants of such dwelling, building, or structure; of the occupants of neighborhood dwellings, buildings, or structures; or of other residents of the city; such conditions may include the following (without limiting the generality of the foregoing): 
(1)	Defects therein increasing the hazards of fire, accidents, or other calamities;
(2)	Lack of adequate ventilation, light, or sanitary facilities;
(3)	Dilapidation;
(4)	Disrepair;
(5)	Structural defects; and
(6)	Uncleanliness.
Sec. 5-33. - Procedure for correcting deficiencies. 
(a)	Whenever a request is filed with the public officer by a public authority or by at least five residents of the city charging that any dwelling, building, or structure is unfit for human habitation or for commercial, industrial, or business use or whenever it appears to the public officer (on his own motion) that any dwelling, building, or structure is unfit for human habitation or is unfit for its current commercial, industrial, or business use, the public officer shall, if his preliminary investigation discloses a basis for such charges, issue and cause to be served upon the owner of and any parties in interest in such dwelling, building, or structure a complaint stating the charges in that respect and containing a notice that a hearing will be held before the municipal court at a place within the county fixed not less than ten days nor more than 30 days after the serving of said complaint; that the owner and any parties in interest shall be given the right to file an answer to the complaint and to appear in person, or otherwise, and give testimony at the place and time fixed in the complaint; and that the rules of evidence prevailing in courts of law or equity shall not be controlling in hearings before the public officer; 
(b)	If, after such notice and hearing, the municipal court determines that the dwelling, building, or structure under consideration is unfit for human habitation or is unfit for its current commercial, industrial, or business use, it shall state in writing its findings of fact in support of such determination and shall issue and cause to be served upon the owner thereof an order: 
(1)	If the repair, alteration, or improvement of the dwelling, building, or structure can be made at a reasonable cost in relation to the value of the dwelling, building, or structure, requiring the owner or parties in interest, within the time specified in the order, to repair, alter, or improve such dwelling, building, or structure so as to render it fit for human habitation or for current commercial, industrial, or business use or to vacate and close the dwelling, building, or structure as a human habitation; or 
(2)	If the repair, alteration, or improvement of the dwelling, building, or structure cannot be made at a reasonable cost in relation to the value of the dwelling, building, or structure, requiring the owner or parties in interest, within the time specified in the order, to remove or demolish such dwelling, building, or structure. 
(3)	For purposes of this section, the court shall make its determination of "reasonable cost in relation to the present value of the dwelling, building, or structure" without consideration of the value of the land on which the structure is situated; provided, however, that costs of the preparation necessary to repair, alter, or improve a structure may be considered. Income and financial status of the owner shall not be factor in the court's determination. The present value of the structure and the costs of repair, alteration, or improvement may be established by affidavits of real estate appraisers with a Georgia appraiser classification as provided in Chapter 39A of Title 43, qualified building contractors, or qualified building inspectors without actual testimony presented. Costs of repair, alteration, or improvement of the structure shall be the cost necessary to bring the structure into compliance with the applicable codes relevant to the cited violations in force in the jurisdiction. 
In no event shall the council require removal or demolition of any dwelling, building, or structure except upon a finding that the cost of repair, alteration, or improvement thereof exceeds one-half the value such dwelling, building, or structure will have when repaired to satisfy the minimum requirements of this law; 
(c)	If the owner or parties in interest fail to comply with an order to vacate and close or demolish the dwelling, building, or structure, the public officer may cause such dwelling, building, or structure to be repaired, altered, or improved or to be vacated and closed or demolished; and that the public officer may cause to be posted on the main entrance of any building, dwelling, or structure so closed a placard with the following words: 
"This building is unfit for human habitation or commercial, industrial, or business use; the use or occupation of this building for human habitation or for commercial, industrial, or business use is prohibited and unlawful." 
(d)	If the owner fails to comply with any order to remove or demolish the dwelling, building, or structure, the public officer may cause such dwelling, building, or structure to be removed or demolished; provided, however, that the duties of the public officer, set forth in the preceding paragraph and this paragraph, shall not be exercised until the council shall have by ordinance ordered the public officer to proceed to effectuate the purpose of this article with respect to the particular property or properties which the public officer shall have found to be unfit for human habitation or unfit for its current commercial, industrial, or business use, which property or properties shall be described in the ordinance. 
(e)	The amount of the cost of such vacating and closing or removal or demolition by the public officer shall be a lien against the real property upon which such cost was incurred. The lien shall attach to the real property upon the payment of all costs of demolition by the municipality and the filing of an itemized statement of the total sum of the costs by the public officer in the office of the clerk on a lien docket maintained by the clerk for such purposes. If the dwelling, building, or structure is removed or demolished by the public officer, he shall sell the materials of such dwellings, buildings, or structures and shall credit the proceeds of such sale against the cost of the removal or demolition and any balance remaining shall be deposited in the superior court by the public officer, shall be secured in such manner as may be directed by such court, and shall be disbursed by such court to the persons found to be entitled thereto by final order or decree of such court. Nothing in this section shall be construed to impair or limit in any way the power of the city to define and declare nuisances and to cause their removal or abatement by summary proceedings or otherwise. 
(f)	The city may enforce the collection of any amount due on such lien for removal or demolition of dwellings, buildings, or structures only in the following manner: 
(1)	The owner or parties at interest shall be allowed to satisfy the amount due on such lien by paying to the city, within 30 days after the perfection of the lien, a sum of money equal to 25 percent of the total amount due and by further paying to the city the remaining balance due on such lien, together with interest at the rate of seven percent per annum, in three equal annual payments, each of which shall become due and payable on the anniversary date of the initial payment made as hereinabove prescribed. 
(2)	Should the property upon which such lien is perfected be sold, transferred, or conveyed by the owner or parties at interest at any time prior to the termination of the three-year period, then the entire balance due on such lien shall be due and payable to the city. 
(3)	Should the amount due on such lien, or any portion thereof, be unpaid after the passage of the three-year period, or upon the occurrence of the contingency provided for in subparagraph (b) of this paragraph, the city may enforce the collection of any amount due on such lien for alteration, repair, removal, or demolition of dwellings, buildings, or structures in the same manner as provided in OCGA § 48-5-358 and other applicable state statutes. This procedure shall be subject to the right of redemption by any person having any right, title, or interest in or lien upon said property, all as provided by Article 3 of Chapter 4 of Title 48, OCGA. 
Sec. 5-34. - Service of complaints or orders. 
(a)	Complaints or orders issued by a public officer shall, in all cases, be served as provided in OCGA § 41-2-12. 
(b)	A copy of such complaint or orders shall be filed in the proper office or offices for the filing of lis pendens notice in the county in which the dwelling, building, or structure is located and such filing of the complaint or orders shall have the same force and effect as other lis pendens notices provided by law. Any such complaint or orders or an appropriate lis pendens notice may contain a statement to the effect that a lien may arise against the described property and that an itemized statement of such lien is maintained on a lien docket maintained by the city clerk. 
Sec. 5-35. - Injunctions against order to repair, close, or demolish unfit buildings or structures. 
Any person affected by an order issued by the public officer or municipal court may petition to the superior court for an injunction restraining the public officer from carrying out the provisions of the order and the court may, upon such petition, issue a temporary injunction restraining the public officer pending the final disposition of the cause; provided, however, that such person shall present such petition to the court within 15 days of the posting and service of the order of the public officer. De novo hearings shall be had by the court on petitions within 20 days. The court shall hear and determine the issues raised and shall enter such final order or decree as law and justice may require; provided, however, that it shall not be necessary to file bond in any amount before obtaining a temporary injunction under this section. 
Sec. 5-36. - Taking of unfit buildings or structures by eminent domain; police power. 
Nothing in this article shall be construed as preventing the owner or owners of any property from receiving just compensation for the taking of such property by the power of eminent domain under the laws of this state nor as permitting any property to be condemned or destroyed except in accordance with the police power of this state. 
Sec. 5-37. - Authority to use revenues, grants, and donations to repair, close, or demolish unfit buildings or structures. 
The city is authorized to make such appropriations from its revenues as it may deem necessary and may accept and apply grants or donations to assist it in carrying out the provisions of this article. 
Sec. 5-38. - Article cumulative. 
This article shall be cumulative of all other remedies of the city provided by law or by the technical codes adopted by the city. 
Sec. 5-39. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - SWIMMING POOLS 

Sec. 5-40. - Definitions. 
As used in this article, the following terms shall have the respective meanings ascribed to them: 
Reconstruction means the replacement of, alteration of, or addition to, an existing swimming pool, but not including equipment. 
Swimming pool means any structure intended for swimming, recreational bathing or wading that contains water over 24 inches deep. This includes in-ground, above-ground and on-ground pools; hot tubs; spas and fixed-in-place wading pools. 
(Ord. No. 105, § I, 9-6-2011)
Sec. 5-41. - Enforcement—Officer designated; inspections required. 
The building inspector shall enforce the provisions of this article, and to that end shall make periodic inspections of all swimming pools. 
Sec. 5-42. - Same—Allowing inspection. 
The owner or other person in possession of any swimming pool shall allow any person charged with the enforcement hereof to inspect the same at reasonable times. 
Sec. 5-43. - Declaration of necessity. 
It is determined and declared that the use of public or private swimming pools in the city without appropriate precautionary safety measures constitutes a hazard to the safety of the residents of the city, particularly children. 
Sec. 5-44. - Same—Noncompliance unlawful.
